\\n293: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\\n294:     /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\\n295:     /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\\n296:     /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\\n297:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\\n302:             }\\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\\n307:                 } else {\\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\\n310:                     let err_args =\\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\\n312:                     ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\\n313:                 };\\n314:                 self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\\n315:             }\\n316:         }\\n317:     }\\n318: }\\n319: \\n320: /// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\\n321: /// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\\n322: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\\n323: /// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\\n324: /// ```\\n325: /// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\\n326: /// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\\n327: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\\n328: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n329: #[cfg_attr(\\n330:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n331:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n332: )]\\n333: pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\\n334:     pub def_id: I::TraitId,\\n335:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n336:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\\n337:     /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\\n338:     _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n339: }\\n340: \\n341: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\\n342: \\n343: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n344:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\\n345:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\\n346:         Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\\n347:     }\\n348: \\n349:     pub fn new(\\n350:         interner: I,\\n351:         trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\\n352:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n353:     ) -> Self {\\n354:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n355:         Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n359:         // Assert there is a Self.\\n360:         trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\\n361: \\n362:         ExistentialTraitRef {\\n363:             def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\\n364:             args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\\n365:             _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n366:         }\\n367:     }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\\n302:             }\\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\\n307:                 } else {\\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\\n310:                     let err_args =\\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\\n312:                     ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\\n313:                 };\\n314:                 self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\\n315:             }\\n316:         }\\n317:     }\\n318: }\\n319: \\n320: /// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\\n321: /// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\\n322: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\\n323: /// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\\n324: /// ```\\n325: /// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\\n326: /// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\\n327: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\\n328: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n329: #[cfg_attr(\\n330:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n331:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n332: )]\\n333: pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\\n334:     pub def_id: I::TraitId,\\n335:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n336:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\\n337:     /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\\n338:     _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n339: }\\n340: \\n341: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\\n342: \\n343: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n344:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\\n345:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\\n346:         Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\\n347:     }\\n348: \\n349:     pub fn new(\\n350:         interner: I,\\n351:         trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\\n352:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n353:     ) -> Self {\\n354:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n355:         Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n359:         // Assert there is a Self.\\n360:         trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\\n361: \\n362:         ExistentialTraitRef {\\n363:             def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\\n364:             args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\\n365:             _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\\n366:         }\\n367:     }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\\n370:     /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\\n371:     /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\\n372:     /// or some placeholder type.\\n373:     pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\\n374:         // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\\n375:         // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\\n376: \\n377:         TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\\n378:     }\\n379: }\\n380: \\n381: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\\n382:     pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\\n383:         self.skip_binder().def_id\\n384:     }\\n385: \\n386:     /// Object types don't have a self type specified. I: Interner)]\\n397: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n398: #[cfg_attr(\\n399:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n400:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n401: )]\\n402: pub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\\n403:     pub def_id: I::DefId,\\n404:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n405:     pub term: I::Term,\\n406: \\n407:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\\n408:     /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\\n409:     use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\\n410: }\\n411: \\n412: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\\n413: \\n414: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n415:     pub fn new_from_args(\\n416:         interner: I,\\n417:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n418:         args: I::GenericArgs,\\n419:         term: I::Term,\\n420:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n421:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\\n422:         Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\\n423:     }\\n424: \\n425:     pub fn new(\\n426:         interner: I,\\n427:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n428:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n429:         term: I::Term,\\n430:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n431:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n432:         Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\\n433:     }\\n434: \\n435:     /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\\n436:     /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\\n437:     /// then this function would return an `exists T. PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as }\\n799: \\n800: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\\n801:     /// Returns the `DefId` of the trait of the associated item being projected.\\n802:     #[inline]\\n803:     pub pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n302:             }\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n306: \n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n488:     ProjectionTy,\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n490:     InherentTy,\n491:     /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n492:     /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n493:     OpaqueTy,\n494:     /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n495:     /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n496:     /// type\",\n513:             AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n514:             AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n515:             AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n516:             AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n517:             AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n518:             AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n519:             AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n520:         }\n521:     }\n522: \n523:     pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n524:         match self {\n525:             AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n526:             | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n527:             | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n528:             |      | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n534:         }\n535:     }\n536: }\n537: \n538: impl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n539:     fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n540:          ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n545:         }\n546:     }\n547: }\n548: \n549: /// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n550: ///\n551: /// * For a projection, ///\n563:     /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n564:     /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n565:     ///\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they /// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\n718: impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n719:     /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as }\n747: \n748: impl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n749:     fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\n750:         AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n751:     }\n752: }\n753: \n754: /// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\n755: /// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\n756: ///\n757: /// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\n758: /// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\n759: ///\n760: /// In particular, form #1 is \"desugared\" to the combination of a\n761: /// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\n762: /// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\n763: /// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\n764: /// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\n765: /// instances to normalize the LHS.\n766: #[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: The central question that usefulness checking answers is:\n10: \"in this match expression, is that branch redundant?\".\n11: More precisely, it boils down to computing whether,\n12: given a list of patterns we have already seen,\n13: a given new pattern might match any new value.\n14: \n15: For example, in the following match expression,\n16: we ask in turn whether each pattern might match something\n17: that wasn't matched by the patterns above it.\n18: Here we see the 4th pattern is redundant with the 1st;\n19: that branch will get an \"unreachable\" warning.\n20: The 3rd pattern may or may not be useful,\n21: depending on whether `Foo` has other variants than `Bar`.\n22: Finally, we can ask whether the whole match is exhaustive\n23: by asking whether the wildcard pattern    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\\n504:     FreeConst,\\n505:     /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\\n506:     InherentConst,\\n507: }\\n508: \\n509: impl These take numerous guises in syntax,\\n44: /// but perhaps the most recognizable form is in a where-clause:\\n45: /// ```ignore (illustrative)\\n46: /// T: Foo<U>\\n47: /// ```\\n48: /// This would Interner)]\\n55: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n56: #[cfg_attr(\\n57:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n58:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, self.args.type_at(0)\\n111:     }\\n112: }\\n113: \\n114: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\\n115:     pub fn self_ty(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\\n116: \\n293: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\\n294:     /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\\n295:     /// self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\\n300:             ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\\n301:                 self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\\n302:             }\\n303:             ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\\n304:                 let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\\n305:                 let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\\n306:                     ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\\n307:                 } else {\\n308:                     // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\\n309:                     // new error args for the missing generics.\\n310:                     let err_args =\\n311:                         GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\\n312: PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, \n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind      | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n534:         }\n535:     }\n536: }\n537: \n538: impl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n539:     fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n540: ///\n563:     /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n564:     /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n565:     ///\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `TraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`TraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for TraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> TraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn from_assoc(interner: I, trait_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        let generics = interner.generics_of(trait_id.into());\n        TraitRef::new(interner, trait_id, args.iter().take(generics.count()))\n    }\n\n    /// Returns a `TraitRef` of the form `P0: Foo<P1..Pn>` where `Pi`\n    /// are the parameters defined on trait.\n    pub fn identity(interner: I, def_id: I::TraitId) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        TraitRef::new_from_args(\n            interner,\n            def_id,\n            I::GenericArgs::identity_for_item(interner, def_id.into()),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        TraitRef::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn self_ty(&self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn self_ty(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\n        self.map_bound_ref(|tr| tr.self_ty())\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_host_effect_clause(self, cx: I, constness: BoundConstness) -> I::Clause {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| {\n            ty::ClauseKind::HostEffect(HostEffectPredicate { trait_ref, constness })\n        })\n        .upcast(cx)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct TraitPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub trait_ref: TraitRef<I>,\n\n    /// If polarity is Positive: we are proving that the trait is implemented.\n    ///\n    /// If polarity is Negative: we are proving that a negative impl of this trait\n    /// exists. (Note that coherence also checks whether negative impls of supertraits\n    /// exist via a series of predicates.)\n    pub polarity: PredicatePolarity,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for TraitPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> TraitPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            trait_ref: TraitPredicate {\n            trait_ref,\n            polarity: PredicatePolarity::Positive,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for TraitPredicate<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum ImplPolarity {\n    /// `impl Trait for Type`\n    Positive,\n    /// `impl !Trait for Type`\n    Negative,\n    /// `#[rustc_reservation_impl] impl Trait for Type`\n    ///\n    /// This is a \"stability hack\", not a real Rust feature.\n    /// See #64631 for details.\n    Reservation,\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for ImplPolarity {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n            Self::Reservation => f.write_str(\"reservation\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl ImplPolarity {\n    /// The polarity marker in front of the impl trait ref if applicable.\n    pub fn as_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => \"\",\n            Self::Negative => \"!\",\n            Self::Reservation => \"\",\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Polarity for a trait predicate. May either be negative or positive.\n/// Distinguished from [`ImplPolarity`] since we never compute goals with\n/// \"reservation\" level.\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum PredicatePolarity {\n    /// `Type: Trait`\n    Positive,\n    /// `Type: !Trait`\n    Negative,\n}\n\nimpl PredicatePolarity {\n    /// Flips polarity by turning `Positive` into `Negative` and `Negative` into `Positive`.\n    pub fn flip(&self) -> PredicatePolarity {\n        match self {\n            PredicatePolarity::Positive => PredicatePolarity::Negative,\n            PredicatePolarity::Negative => PredicatePolarity::Positive,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for PredicatePolarity {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum ExistentialPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    /// E.g., `Iterator`.\n    Trait(ExistentialTraitRef<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Iterator::Item = T`.\n    Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Send`.\n    AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\n    /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\n    /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n        match self.skip_binder() {\n            ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n            ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n                self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n            }\n            ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n                let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n                let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n                    ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n                } else {\n                    // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n                    // new error args for the missing generics.\n                    let err_args =\n                        GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n                    ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n                };\n                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n    /// reference.\n    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n        match value {\n            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n    ///\n    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n    /// if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n    /// this is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n            }\n        }\n        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n                interner,\n                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n            )\n            .into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        assert!(\n            matches!(\n                self.kind(interner),\n                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            ),\n            \"expected a projection\"\n        );\n        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n err_args)\n                };\n                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n    /// reference.\n    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n        match value {\n            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n    ///\n    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n    /// if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n    /// this is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n            }\n        }\n        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n                interner,\n                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n            )\n            .into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        assert!(\n            matches!(\n                self.kind(interner),\n                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            ),\n            \"expected a projection\"\n        );\n        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as Iterator>::Item`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: Iterator` trait reference.\n    ///\n    /// WARNING: This will drop the args for generic associated types\n    /// consider calling [Self::trait_ref_and_own_args] to get those\n    /// as well.\n    pub fn trait_ref(self, interner: I) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).0\n    }\n\n    /// Extract the own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return the slice `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn own_args(self, interner: I) -> I::GenericArgsSlice {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).1\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as the base and the GAT args on top of that.\n    ///\n    /// Does the following transformation:\n    ///\n    /// ```text\n    /// [Self, P_0...P_m] -> [I_0...I_n, P_0...P_m]\n    ///\n    ///     I_i impl args\n    ///     P_j GAT args\n    /// ```\n    pub fn rebase_inherent_args_onto_impl(\n        self,\n        impl_args: I::GenericArgs,\n        interner: I,\n    ) -> I::GenericArgs {\n        debug_assert!(matches!(\n            self.kind(interner),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n        ));\n        interner.mk_args_from_iter(impl_args.iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::AliasTy<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ty: ty::AliasTy<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ty.args, def_id: ty.def_id, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\n/// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\n/// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\n///\n/// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\n/// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\n///\n/// In particular, form #1 is \"desugared\" to the combination of a\n/// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\n/// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\n/// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\n/// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\n/// instances to normalize the LHS.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ProjectionPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub projection_term: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ProjectionPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.projection_term.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        Self {\n            projection_term: self.projection_term.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty),\n            ..self\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.projection_term.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Returns the `DefId` of the trait of the associated item being projected.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn trait_def_id(&self, cx: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.trait_def_id(cx)\n    }\n\n    pub fn term(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Term> {\n        self.map_bound(|predicate| predicate.term)\n    }\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` for the associated type.\n    ///\n    /// Note that this is not the `DefId` of the `TraitRef` containing this\n    /// associated type, which is in `tcx.associated_item(projection_def_id()).container`.\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"ProjectionPredicate({:?}, {:?})\", self.projection_term, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Used by the new solver to normalize an alias. This always expects the `term` to\n/// be an unconstrained inference variable which is used as the output.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct NormalizesTo<I: Interner> {\n    pub alias: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for NormalizesTo<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> NormalizesTo<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.alias.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> NormalizesTo<I> {\n        Self { alias: self.alias.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.alias.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.alias.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for NormalizesTo<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"NormalizesTo({:?}, {:?})\", self.alias, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Encodable_NoContext, Decodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct HostEffectPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub trait_ref: ty::TraitRef<I>,\n    pub constness: BoundConstness,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for HostEffectPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> HostEffectPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.trait_ref.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        Self { trait_ref: self.trait_ref.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.trait_ref.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, HostEffectPredicate<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().def_id()\n    }\n\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.self_ty())\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn constness(self) -> BoundConstness {\n        self.skip_binder().constness\n    }\n}\n\n/// Encodes that `sub_ty` must be a subtype of `super_ty`.
